USER:
#assignflow :Lab 2
Promises and Error Handling Challenge
Scenario
You are developing an e-commerce dashboard that fetches data from various APIs, including a product catalog, user reviews, and a sales report. Each API call could potentially fail due to network issues, incorrect endpoints, or data inconsistencies. To build a stable and user-friendly application, you need to manage these scenarios with proper error handling.

Task
In this lab, you will build a small application that leverages asynchronous API calls using Promises. You will also implement error handling to ensure that the application can manage unexpected issues gracefully. This lab will test your ability to work with asynchronous programming concepts, as well as to manage errors effectively in a real-world scenario.

Objectives
By the end of this lab, you will be able to:

Apply Promises to manage multiple asynchronous operations in JavaScript.
Implement chained Promises to handle sequential data retrieval and manage dependencies between API calls.
Utilize .catch() and .finally() to handle errors and perform cleanup tasks in a Promise chain.
Design custom error classes to improve error identification and debugging.
Implement a retry mechanism to manage failed asynchronous requests, enhancing application resilience.
Analyze the benefits and challenges of using error handling strategies in complex asynchronous workflows.
Instructions
Part 1: Set Up Your Project
Create a New Project:

Set up a new project folder, initialize it with npm init -y, and install any necessary dependencies, such as TypeScript.
Create an apiSimulator.ts file:

This file will contain functions that simulate API requests using Promises.
Each function should return a Promise that resolves with mock data after a delay, or rejects with an error message.
Part 2: Implement API Simulation Functions
Simulate Asynchronous API Calls:

Create the following functions in apiSimulator.ts, ensuring each returns a Promise:

fetchProductCatalog(): Simulates fetching a list of products, each with id, name, and price.
Resolve the Promise with an array of mock products after a 1-second delay.
Use Math.random() to sometimes reject the Promise with an error message, e.g., "Failed to fetch product catalog".
Example Code for fetchProductCatalog()


export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<{ id: number; name: string; price: number }[]> => {
    return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
        if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
            { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200 },
            { id: 2, name: "Headphones", price: 200 },
        ]);
        } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
        }
    }, 1000);
    });
};
Continue with fetchProductReviews() and fetchSalesReport() functions similarly, adding realistic mock data and a chance for rejection.

fetchProductReviews(productId: number): Simulates fetching reviews for a product.

Resolve the Promise with an array of reviews after a 1.5-second delay.
Reject the Promise randomly with an error message, e.g., "Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}".
fetchSalesReport(): Simulates fetching a sales report with totalSales, unitsSold, and averagePrice.

Resolve the Promise with a mock sales report after a 1-second delay.
Reject randomly with an error message, e.g., "Failed to fetch sales report".
Part 3: Build the Main Application Logic
Create an index.ts file to contain the main logic of your application.

Write a Function to Handle API Calls and Display Data:

Use fetchProductCatalog() to fetch product details and display them.
For each product, fetch the reviews using fetchProductReviews(productId).
After fetching products and reviews, retrieve the sales report using fetchSalesReport().
Implement Error Handling Using Promises:

Use .catch() to handle any errors from fetchProductCatalog(), fetchProductReviews(), and fetchSalesReport().
Display error messages to the console if any of the calls fail.
Use .finally() to log a message indicating that all API calls have been attempted.
Part 4: Custom Error Classes
Create Custom Error Classes for different error scenarios:
NetworkError for network-related issues.
DataError for data-related issues (e.g., missing fields in the API response).
Update API Simulation Functions to use these custom error classes when rejecting Promises.
Part 5: Optional Challenge
Create a Retry Mechanism:

Write a utility function retryPromise that accepts an async function, the number of retry attempts, and the delay between attempts.
Hint: Use setTimeout to delay the next attempt.
Hint: You will need to utilize recursion to implement this function. Not sure what recursion is, or don’t quite remember? This is an opportunity to practice your research abilities or review!
Use this function to retry API calls that fail initially.
Implement retryPromise with API Calls to retry up to three times for each API call before giving up.

Critical Thinking Questions
Why is it important to handle errors for each individual API call rather than just at the end of the promise chain?
How does using custom error classes improve debugging and error identification?
When might a retry mechanism be more effective than an immediate failure response?

}

### 📄 `apiSimulator.ts`

```ts
// src/apiSimulator.ts
export class NetworkError extends Error {
  constructor(message: string) {
    super(message);
    this.name = 'NetworkError';
  }
}

export class DataError extends Error {
  constructor(message: string) {
    super(message);
    this.name = 'DataError';
  }
}

export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<{ id: number; name: string; price: number }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200 },
          { id: 2, name: "Headphones", price: 200 },
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(new NetworkError("Failed to fetch product catalog"));
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

export const fetchProductReviews = (productId: number): Promise<{ reviewId: number; rating: number; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { reviewId: 1, rating: 5, comment: "Excellent!" },
          { reviewId: 2, rating: 4, comment: "Very good" },
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(new DataError(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`));
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{ totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({ totalSales: 50000, unitsSold: 200, averagePrice: 250 });
      } else {
        reject(new NetworkError("Failed to fetch sales report"));
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

---

### 📄 `retryPromise.ts`

```ts
// src/retryPromise.ts
export const retryPromise = async <T>(fn: () => Promise<T>, retries: number, delay: number): Promise<T> => {
  try {
    return await fn();
  } catch (error) {
    if (retries === 0) throw error;
    await new Promise((res) => setTimeout(res, delay));
    return retryPromise(fn, retries - 1, delay);
  }
};
```

---

### 📄 `index.ts`

```ts
// src/index.ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport, NetworkError, DataError } from './apiSimulator';
import { retryPromise } from './retryPromise';

const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);
    console.log("Products:", products);

    for (const product of products) {
      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);
        console.log(`Reviews for ${product.name}:`, reviews);
      } catch (err) {
        console.error(`Error fetching reviews for product ${product.name}:`, err);
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      console.log("Sales Report:", report);
    } catch (err) {
      console.error("Error fetching sales report:", err);
    }
  } catch (err) {
    console.error("General error in main flow:", err);
  } finally {
    console.log("All API calls have been attempted.");
  }
};

main();
```

### ✅ Step-by-Step: Project Initialization

---

#### 1. **Create the Project Folder**

```bash
mkdir ecommerce-dashboard
cd ecommerce-dashboard
```

---

#### 2. **Initialize NPM**

```bash
npm init -y
```

This creates `package.json`.

---

#### 3. **Install TypeScript and Node Types**

```bash
npm install typescript @types/node --save-dev
```

---

#### 4. **Create tsconfig.json**

```bash
npx tsc --init
```

Then update it for Node.js projects:

```json
{
  "compilerOptions": {
    "target": "ES6",
    "module": "CommonJS",
    "rootDir": "./src",
    "outDir": "./dist",
    "strict": true,
    "esModuleInterop": true,
    "forceConsistentCasingInFileNames": true,
    "skipLibCheck": true
  }
}
```

---

#### 5. **Create Folder Structure**

```bash
mkdir src
touch src/index.ts src/apiSimulator.ts src/retryPromise.ts
touch README.md TUTORIAL.md
```

---

### ✅ Git & GitHub Setup

---

#### 6. **Initialize Git & First Commit**

```bash
git init
echo "node_modules/\ndist/" > .gitignore
git add .
git commit -m "Initialize project with folder structure and config"
```

#### 7. **Create GitHub Repository**

- Create a new repository on GitHub named `ecommerce-dashboard`
- Add remote and push:

```bash
git remote add origin https://github.com/your-username/ecommerce-dashboard.git
git branch -M main
git push -u origin main
```

---

### ✅ Scripts in `package.json`

In `package.json`, add:

```json
"scripts": {
  "build": "tsc",
  "start": "node dist/index.js",
  "dev": "tsc && node dist/index.js"
}
```


```
├── public/
```

```html
<!-- public/index.html -->
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
  <meta charset="UTF-8" />
  <title>E-Commerce Dashboard</title>
</head>
<body>
  <h1>E-Commerce Dashboard</h1>
  <div id="output">Loading...</div>

  <script type="module" src="../src/frontend.ts"></script>
</body>
</html>
```

---

### 📄 Step 4: Create `frontend.ts`

```ts
// src/frontend.ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from './apiSimulator';
import { retryPromise } from './retryPromise';

const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

const render = (html: string) => {
  output.innerHTML += `<pre>${html}</pre>`;
};

const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);
    render(`Products:\n${JSON.stringify(products, null, 2)}`);

    for (const product of products) {
      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);
        render(`Reviews for ${product.name}:\n${JSON.stringify(reviews, null, 2)}`);
      } catch (err) {
        render(`Error fetching reviews for ${product.name}:\n${err}`);
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      render(`Sales Report:\n${JSON.stringify(report, null, 2)}`);
    } catch (err) {
      render(`Error fetching sales report:\n${err}`);
    }
  } catch (err) {
    render(`Fatal Error:\n${err}`);
  }
};

main();
```

---

### 🛠 Step 5: Update `package.json` Scripts

```json
"scripts": {
  "dev": "parcel public/index.html",
  "build": "parcel build public/index.html"
}
```

---

### 🚀 Step 6: Run Your App

```bash
npm run dev
```

Visit `http://localhost:1234` in your browser.

USER:
which one is cleaner and complies with the best practices

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
### ✅ Best Practice Recommendation: **Option 1 — Flatten the Structure**

---

### 🔎 Why Option 1 is Cleaner and Preferred

| Criteria | Option 1: Move files to root | Option 2: Use nested folder |
|---------|------------------------------|-----------------------------|
| ✅ **Clarity** | Everything lives at the project root — intuitive and clean | Easy to get lost in subfolders |
| ✅ **Simplicity** | One `package.json`, one terminal path | Requires remembering to `cd` into subfolders |
| ✅ **Tool compatibility** | Tools like Parcel, Vite, GitHub Actions expect root structure | May require path adjustments |
| ✅ **Collaboration** | New developers see a standard layout | Nonstandard nesting adds friction |
| ✅ **Docs & Deployment** | Matches most tutorials and deployment pipelines | Extra nesting may break configs |

---

### 🧼 Option 1: Cleaner Folder Layout

```bash
ecommerce_dashboard_frontend/
├── public/
│   └── index.html
├── src/
│   ├── frontend.ts
│   ├── apiSimulator.ts
│   ├── retryPromise.ts
│   └── index.ts
├── .gitignore
├── package.json
├── tsconfig.json
└── README.md
```

ASSISTANT:
Thanks — an empty console with `"Loading..."` stuck usually means **the JavaScript bundle isn't loading or running at all**. Let’s check and fix this fast:

---

### ✅ Fix 1: Move the `<script>` to `index.html` Properly

You’re using:

```html
<script type="module" src="../src/frontend.ts"></script>
```

This works **only if the file is reachable from that relative path**. With Parcel, the correct and reliable way is:

```html
<script type="module" src="/src/frontend.ts"></script>
```

💡 `Parcel` rewrites `/src/frontend.ts` into a valid JS bundle — no need for `../`.

---

### ✅ Fix 2: Restart Parcel Dev Server

Sometimes Parcel doesn’t pick up new files properly until restarted. Run:

```bash
Ctrl + C   # to stop the current server
npm run dev
```

---

### ✅ Fix 3: Ensure Parcel Compiles TypeScript

Make sure you do **not** manually compile with `tsc` — Parcel handles `.ts` natively.

If you see `dist/` from previous builds, you can delete it:

```bash
rm -r dist
```

---

### Bonus Check

Make sure this element exists in `index.html`:

```html
<div id="output">Loading...</div>
```

If it has a different ID, the script can’t find it and silently fails.

Let me know when these are updated or upload your current `index.html` and `frontend.ts` if you'd like me to double-check directly.

import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from './apiSimulator';
import { retryPromise } from './retryPromise';

const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

const render = (html: string) => {
  const pre = document.createElement('pre');
  pre.textContent = html;
  output.appendChild(pre);
};

const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);
    render(`Products:\n${JSON.stringify(products, null, 2)}`);

      } catch (err) {
        render(`Error fetching reviews for ${product.name}: ${err}`);

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
Great — thanks for sharing your current `frontend.ts`. You're absolutely right: this version doesn't apply any of the CSS class names like `card`, `review`, `error`, or `card-title`. That's why your layout appears unstyled.

---

### ✅ Here’s the Fixed Version (With Class-Based Rendering)

Replace your current `frontend.ts` with this updated version:

```ts
// src/frontend.ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from './apiSimulator';
import { retryPromise } from './retryPromise';

const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

/**
 * Render a block of content with optional styling.
 * @param html - The HTML content to display.
 * @param className - CSS class to apply for styling (defaults to 'card').
 */
const render = (html: string, className: string = "card") => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = className;
  div.innerHTML = `<pre>${html}</pre>`;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);
    render("Products:", "card-title");
    render(JSON.stringify(products, null, 2)); // uses default "card" style

    for (const product of products) {
      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);
        render(`Reviews for ${product.name}:`, "card-title");
        reviews.forEach(review => {
          render(JSON.stringify(review, null, 2), "review");
        });
      } catch (err) {
        render(`Error fetching reviews for ${product.name}:\n${err}`, "error");
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      render("Sales Report:", "card-title");
      render(JSON.stringify(report, null, 2)); // uses default "card" style
    } catch (err) {
      render(`Error fetching sales report:\n${err}`, "error");
    }
  } catch (err) {
    render(`Fatal Error:\n${err}`, "error");
  }
};

main();
```

---

2. Run `npm run dev`
3. Refresh [http://localhost:1234](http://localhost:1234)

You should now see styled sections — blue titles, white cards, green reviews, red errors.

### ✅ Best Practice: Preserve This Version, Refactor Separately with Tailwind

Here’s why:

| Reason | Why It Matters |
|--------|----------------|
| ✅ **Version Control** | Keeps your current vanilla CSS version clean and working |
| ✅ **Learning Clarity** | You’ll clearly see what Tailwind improves, reuses, or simplifies |
| ✅ **Clean Fork Path** | You avoid messy conditionals or CSS bloat mixing two styles |
| ✅ **Better Comparison** | You'll be able to compare final results side-by-side for learning/reporting |
| ✅ **GitHub/Grading Ready** | You can tag/branch this version as `v1-css` and start a fresh fork as `v2-tailwind` |

---

### 👌 Recommendation

- Keep this version **as-is** (with minor polish only).
- Create a **new GitHub fork or branch** for the **Tailwind challenge**.
- Start the Tailwind fork clean: no external CSS, use utility classes only.

- Padding
- Table layout or flexbox
- Proper spacing

---

### ✅ Step 3: Replace JSON Output

Instead of:
```ts
render(JSON.stringify(product, null, 2));
```

We’ll generate:
```html
<div class="card">
  <h2>Laptop</h2>
  <p>Price: $1200</p>
</div>
```

### 🧪 What You’ll See After

- Product cards with clean fields
- Review comments in rows
- Sales report in a stats box or table
- Readable, structured layout

      "pattern": ".*",

name: string; price: number }) => {\n  const card = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  card.className = \"card\";\n  card.innerHTML = `\n    <h2 class=\"card-title\">${product.name}</h2>\n    <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(card);\n};\n\nconst renderReview = (review: any) => {\n  const div = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  div.className = \"review\";\n  div.innerHTML = `\n    <p><strong>${review.author || 'Anonymous'}:</strong> ${review.comment || 'No comment provided'}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(div);\n};\n\nconst renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {\n  const card = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  card.className = \"card\";\n  card.innerHTML = `\n    <h2 class=\"card-title\">Sales Report</h2>\n    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>\n    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>\n    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(card);\n};\n\nconst renderError = (message: string) => {\n  const div = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  div.className = \"error\";\n  div.textContent = message;\n  output.appendChild(div);\n};\n\nconst main = async () => {\n  try {\n    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);\n\n    products.forEach(product => {\n      renderProductCard(product);\n    });\n\n    for (const product of products) {\n      try {\n        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);\n        if (reviews.length > 0) {\n          const title = document.createElement(\"h3\");\n          title.className = \"card-title\";\n          title.textContent = `Reviews for ${product.name}`;\n          output.appendChild(title);\n        }\n        reviews.forEach(renderReview);\n      } catch (err) {\n        renderError(`Error fetching reviews for ${product.name}:\\n${err}`);\n      }\n    }\n\n    try {\n      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);\n      renderSalesReport(report);\n    } catch (err) {\n      renderError(`Error fetching sales report:\\n${err}`);\n    }\n  } catch (err) {\n    renderError(`Fatal Error:\\n${err}`);\n  }\n};\n\nmain();"
    }
  ]
}

name: string; price: number }) => {\n  const card = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  card.className = \"card\";\n  card.innerHTML = `\n    <h2 class=\"card-title\">${product.name}</h2>\n    <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(card);\n};\n\n/**\n * Render a single review comment block\n */\nconst renderReview = (review: any) => {\n  const div = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  div.className = \"review\";\n  div.innerHTML = `\n    <p><strong>${review.author || 'Anonymous'}:</strong> ${review.comment || 'No comment provided'}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(div);\n};\n\n/**\n * Render a clean, formatted sales report\n */\nconst renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {\n  const card = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  card.className = \"card\";\n  card.innerHTML = `\n    <h2 class=\"card-title\">Sales Report</h2>\n    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>\n    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>\n    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(card);\n};\n\n/**\n * Render a clean error message box\n */\nconst renderError = (message: string) => {\n  const div = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  div.className = \"error\";\n  div.textContent = message;\n  output.appendChild(div);\n};\n\n/**\n * Main function to orchestrate fetching and rendering of data\n */\nconst main = async () => {\n  try {\n    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);\n\n    products.forEach(product => {\n      renderProductCard(product);\n    });\n\n    for (const product of products) {\n      try {\n        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);\n        if (reviews.length > 0) {\n          const title = document.createElement(\"h3\");\n          title.className = \"card-title\";\n          title.textContent = `Reviews for ${product.name}`;\n          output.appendChild(title);\n        }\n        reviews.forEach(renderReview);\n      } catch (err) {\n        renderError(`Error fetching reviews for ${product.name}:\\n${err}`);\n      }\n    }\n\n    try {\n      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);\n      renderSalesReport(report);\n    } catch (err) {\n      renderError(`Error fetching sales report:\\n${err}`);\n    }\n  } catch (err) {\n    renderError(`Fatal Error:\\n${err}`);\n  }\n};\n\n// Run the application\nmain();"

name: string; price: number }) => {\n  const card = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  card.className = \"card\";\n  card.innerHTML = `\n    <h2 class=\"card-title\">${product.name}</h2>\n    <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(card);\n};\n\n// Renders a review section under the product\nconst renderReview = (review: any) => {\n  const div = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  div.className = \"review\";\n  div.innerHTML = `\n    <p><strong>${review.author || 'Anonymous'}:</strong> ${review.comment || 'No comment provided'}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(div);\n};\n\n// Renders a formatted sales report at the end\nconst renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {\n  const card = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  card.className = \"card\";\n  card.innerHTML = `\n    <h2 class=\"card-title\">Sales Report</h2>\n    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>\n    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>\n    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(card);\n};\n\n// Renders error messages in a styled alert box\nconst renderError = (message: string) => {\n  const div = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  div.className = \"error\";\n  div.textContent = message;\n  output.appendChild(div);\n};\n\n// Main function to orchestrate all API calls and render outputs\nconst main = async () => {\n  try {\n    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);\n\n    products.forEach(product => {\n      renderProductCard(product);\n    });\n\n    for (const product of products) {\n      try {\n        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);\n\n        if (reviews.length > 0) {\n          // Title for the review section per product\n          const title = document.createElement(\"h3\");\n          title.className = \"card-title\";\n          title.textContent = `Reviews for ${product.name}`;\n          output.appendChild(title);\n        }\n\n        // Render each review under the product\n        reviews.forEach(renderReview);\n      } catch (err) {\n        renderError(`Error fetching reviews for ${product.name}:\\n${err}`);\n      }\n    }\n\n    try {\n      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);\n      renderSalesReport(report);\n    } catch (err) {\n      renderError(`Error fetching sales report:\\n${err}`);\n    }\n  } catch (err) {\n    renderError(`Fatal Error:\\n${err}`);\n  }\n};\n\nmain();"
    }
  ]

name: string; price: number }) => {\n  const card = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  card.className = \"card\";\n  card.innerHTML = `\n    <h2 class=\"card-title\">${product.name}</h2>\n    <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>\n    <div class=\"reviews\" id=\"reviews-${product.id}\"></div>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(card);\n};\n\n// Renders a review under its respective product card\nconst renderReview = (review: any, productId: number) => {\n  const reviewsContainer = document.getElementById(`reviews-${productId}`);\n  if (reviewsContainer) {\n    const div = document.createElement(\"div\");\n    div.className = \"review\";\n    div.innerHTML = `\n      <p><strong>${review.author || 'Anonymous'}:</strong> ${review.comment || 'No comment provided'}</p>\n    `;\n    reviewsContainer.appendChild(div);\n  }\n};\n\n// Renders a formatted sales report at the end\nconst renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {\n  const card = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  card.className = \"card\";\n  card.innerHTML = `\n    <h2 class=\"card-title\">Sales Report</h2>\n    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>\n    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>\n    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(card);\n};\n\n// Renders error messages in a styled alert box\nconst renderError = (message: string) => {\n  const div = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  div.className = \"error\";\n  div.textContent = message;\n  output.appendChild(div);\n};\n\n// Main function to orchestrate all API calls and render outputs\nconst main = async () => {\n  try {\n    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);\n\n    products.forEach(product => {\n      renderProductCard(product);\n    });\n\n    for (const product of products) {\n      try {\n        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);\n\n        // Render each review under the product card\n        reviews.forEach(review => renderReview(review, product.id));\n\n      } catch (err) {\n        renderError(`Error fetching reviews for ${product.name}:\\n${err}`);\n      }\n    }\n\n    try {\n      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);\n      renderSalesReport(report);\n    } catch (err) {\n      renderError(`Error fetching sales report:\\n${err}`);\n    }\n  } catch (err) {\n    renderError(`Fatal Error:\\n${err}`);\n  }\n};\n\nmain();"

      "replacement": "// src/frontend.ts\n// Import necessary modules for data fetching and retry logic\nimport { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from './apiSimulator';\nimport { retryPromise } from './retryPromise';\n\n// Select the output container in the DOM where all content will be rendered\nconst output = document.getElementById(\"output\")!;\n\n/**\n * Renders a product card displaying the product name and price.\n * Also creates a placeholder container for that product's reviews.\n */\nconst renderProductCard = (product: { id: number; name: string; price: number }) => {\n  const card = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  card.className = \"card\";\n  card.innerHTML = `\n    <h2 class=\"card-title\">${product.name}</h2>\n    <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>\n    <div class=\"reviews\" id=\"reviews-${product.id}\"></div>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(card);\n};\n\n/**\n * Renders a review for a specific product by appending it to the product's review container.\n */\nconst renderReview = (review: any, productId: number) => {\n  const reviewsContainer = document.getElementById(`reviews-${productId}`);\n  if (reviewsContainer) {\n    const div = document.createElement(\"div\");\n    div.className = \"review\";\n    div.innerHTML = `\n      <p><strong>${review.author || 'Anonymous'}:</strong> ${review.comment || 'No comment provided'}</p>\n    `;\n    reviewsContainer.appendChild(div);\n  }\n};\n\n/**\n * Renders a formatted card showing sales statistics.\n */\nconst renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {\n  const card = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  card.className = \"card\";\n  card.innerHTML = `\n    <h2 class=\"card-title\">Sales Report</h2>\n    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>\n    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>\n    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>\n  `;\n  output.appendChild(card);\n};\n\n/**\n * Renders an error message styled as an alert box.\n */\nconst renderError = (message: string) => {\n  const div = document.createElement(\"div\");\n  div.className = \"error\";\n  div.textContent = message;\n  output.appendChild(div);\n};\n\n/**\n * Main function to orchestrate fetching and rendering products, reviews, and sales report.\n * Uses retryPromise to add robustness against transient errors.\n */\nconst main = async () => {\n  try {\n    // Fetch and render product catalog\n    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);\n\n    products.forEach(product => {\n      renderProductCard(product); // Render product UI\n    });\n\n    for (const product of products) {\n      try {\n        // Fetch and render reviews for each product\n        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);\n        reviews.forEach(review => renderReview(review, product.id));\n      } catch (err) {\n        renderError(`Error fetching reviews for ${product.name}:\\n${err}`);\n      }\n    }\n\n    try {\n      // Fetch and render the overall sales report\n      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);\n      renderSalesReport(report);\n    } catch (err) {\n      renderError(`Error fetching sales report:\\n${err}`);\n    }\n  } catch (err) {\n    // Catch fatal errors that may occur before any rendering begins\n    renderError(`Fatal Error:\\n${err}`);\n  }\n};\n\n// Execute the main workflow\nmain();"
    }
  ]
}

// Render product UI\n    });\n\n    for (const product of products) {\n      try {\n        // Fetch reviews for each product\n        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);\n\n        // If reviews exist, add a \"Reviews\" header\n        if (reviews.length > 0) {\n          const reviewsContainer = document.getElementById(`reviews-${product.id}`);\n          if (reviewsContainer) {\n            const title = document.createElement(\"h3\");\n            title.className = \"review-title\";\n            title.textContent = \"Reviews\";\n            reviewsContainer.appendChild(title);\n          }\n        }\n\n        // Render each review under the corresponding product card\n        reviews.forEach(review => renderReview(review, product.id));\n\n      } catch (err) {\n        renderError(`Error fetching reviews for ${product.name}:\\n${err}`);\n      }\n    }\n\n    try {\n      // Fetch and render the overall sales report\n      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);\n      renderSalesReport(report);\n    } catch (err) {\n      renderError(`Error fetching sales report:\\n${err}`);\n    }\n  } catch (err) {\n    // Catch fatal errors that may occur before any rendering begins\n    renderError(`Fatal Error:\\n${err}`);\n  }\n};\n\n// Execute the main workflow\nmain();"
    }
  ]
}

USER:
will the images be stored in the source folder  or should we make an assects folder?, suggest the best option based on best practices

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
Excellent question — you're thinking like a seasoned developer. Here’s the best practice breakdown:

---

### ✅ Recommended Practice: Use an `assets/` Folder

**Why?**

| ✅ Benefit | Explanation |
|-----------|-------------|
| **Organized** | Keeps images, icons, and static files separate from logic (TS/JS code) |
| **Scalable** | Easy to manage dozens or hundreds of images in a single folder |
| **Clear Purpose** | `src/` is meant for logic/code — `assets/` is meant for static files |
| **Framework Friendly** | Most tools (Parcel, Vite, Webpack) expect `assets/` or `public/` folders for this purpose |

---

### 📁 Suggested Structure

```
ecommerce_dashboard_frontend/
├── public/
│   ├── index.html
├── src/
│   ├── frontend.ts
│   ├── ...
├── assets/         ✅ Put your images here
│   ├── laptop.png
│   ├── headphones.png
```

Then reference them like:

```ts
<img src="/assets/laptop.png" alt="Laptop" />
```

Parcel will resolve this correctly.

---

```ts
// src/apiSimulator.ts

export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<{ id: number; name: string; price: number; image: string }[]> => {

    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

```ts
// src/apiSimulator.ts

// Define a product structure that includes an image path
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<{ id: number; name: string; price: number; image: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          {
            id: 1,
            name: "Laptop",
            price: 1200,
            image: "./assets/laptop2.png"
          },
          {
            id: 2,
            name: "Headphones",
            price: 200,
            image: "./assets/headphone1.png"
          }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

// Simulate fetching reviews for a given product
export const fetchProductReviews = (productId: number): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`);
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

// Simulate fetching a sales report
export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{ totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({
          totalSales: 50000,
          unitsSold: 250,
          averagePrice: 200
        });
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch sales report");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
Excellent! Let’s update `frontend.ts` to render each product as a **card** that includes:

- 🖼 Product image (from `image` path)
- 🏷 Name and price
- 🗣 Reviews below a “Reviews” header (if available)

Here’s your updated, ready-to-paste `frontend.ts` file:

```ts
// src/frontend.ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from './apiSimulator';
import { retryPromise } from './retryPromise';

// Grab the output container
const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

/**
 * Renders a review message inside a product container
 */
const renderReview = (productDiv: HTMLElement, reviewText: string, className: string = "review") => {
  const reviewDiv = document.createElement("div");
  reviewDiv.className = className;
  reviewDiv.textContent = reviewText;
  productDiv.appendChild(reviewDiv);
};

/**
 * Renders a full product card with image, details, and space for reviews
 */
const renderProductCard = (product: { id: number; name: string; price: number; image: string }) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";

  card.innerHTML = `
    <div class="card-content">
      <img src="${product.image}" alt="${product.name}" class="product-image" />
      <div class="product-details">
        <h2>${product.name}</h2>
        <p>Price: $${product.price}</p>
        <h3>Reviews:</h3>
      </div>
    </div>
  `;

  output.appendChild(card);
  return card.querySelector(".product-details") as HTMLElement; // We’ll append reviews here
};

/**
 * Renders the sales report at the end of the dashboard
 */
const renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p>Total Sales: $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p>Units Sold: ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p>Average Price: $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

/**
 * Renders error messages with visual distinction
 */
const renderError = (message: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = message;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

/**
 * Main workflow: fetch products, render cards, fetch reviews, then sales report
 */
const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);

    for (const product of products) {
      const productCard = renderProductCard(product);

      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);

        if (reviews.length === 0) {
          renderReview(productCard, "No reviews yet.");
        } else {
          reviews.forEach((review) => {
            renderReview(productCard, `💬 ${review.user}: ${review.comment}`);
          });
        }

      } catch (err) {
        renderReview(productCard, `⚠️ Error loading reviews: ${err}`, "error");
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(`Error fetching sales report: ${err}`);
    }

  } catch (err) {
    renderError(`Fatal Error: ${err}`);
  }
};

// Start app
main();
```

---

### 🔍 Why the Images Aren’t Showing

Parcel **does not serve `assets/` from the root by default**. So the image path `./assets/laptop2.png` is **relative to `index.html` inside `public/`**, which won't work without special handling.

---

### ✅ Fix: Move Assets to `public/assets/`

**Best Practice for Parcel:**
Place images in the `public/` folder — which **does get served directly**.

---

### 📁 New Structure

Move your images to:

```
public/assets/
├── laptop2.png
├── headphone1.png
```

Then update the image path in `apiSimulator.ts` like this:

```ts
image: "/assets/laptop2.png"
```

and

```ts
image: "/assets/headphone1.png"
```

**Notice the `/` at the beginning** — this tells Parcel to treat it as a static asset from the public root.

---

### 🔁 Then:

1. Save changes to `apiSimulator.ts`
2. Run:

ASSISTANT:
Thanks for the screenshot — the issue is clear.

---

### ❌ Problem

You're trying to define a **type inline** inside the return type of the function, like this:

```ts
(): Promise<{ id: number; name: string; price: number; image: string }> => { ... }
```

Which is valid TypeScript, **but only if it’s in a `.ts` file with correct TypeScript config**.

---

### ✅ Fix Options

#### Option 1: (✅ Best Practice)
Move the inline type to a **reusable interface**.

Update `apiSimulator.ts` like this:

```ts
// Define a Product type
export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
  image: string;
}

// Return type now uses the interface
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          {
            id: 1,
            name: "Laptop",
            price: 1200,
            image: "/assets/laptop2.png"
          },
          {
            id: 2,
            name: "Headphones",
            price: 200,
            image: "/assets/headphone1.png"
          }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

Then in `frontend.ts`, update the render function type if necessary:

```ts
import type { Product } from "./apiSimulator";

// Now you can write:
const renderProductCard = (product: Product) => { ... }
```

write the frontend .ts for copy and paste with the update changes

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
Absolutely! Here's your fully updated, clean, and well-commented `frontend.ts` file to support image rendering and use the shared `Product` interface:

```ts
// src/frontend.ts
import {
  fetchProductCatalog,
  fetchProductReviews,
  fetchSalesReport,
  Product, // ✅ Import the Product type
} from "./apiSimulator";
import { retryPromise } from "./retryPromise";

// Grab the output container
const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

/**
 * Renders an individual review inside the appropriate product card.
 */
const renderReview = (
  productDetailsDiv: HTMLElement,
  reviewText: string,
  className: string = "review"
) => {
  const reviewDiv = document.createElement("div");
  reviewDiv.className = className;
  reviewDiv.textContent = reviewText;
  productDetailsDiv.appendChild(reviewDiv);
};

/**
 * Renders a complete product card including image, name, price, and review section.
 */
const renderProductCard = (product: Product): HTMLElement => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";

  card.innerHTML = `
    <div class="card-content">
      <img src="${product.image}" alt="${product.name}" class="product-image" />
      <div class="product-details">
        <h2>${product.name}</h2>
        <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
        <h3>Reviews:</h3>
      </div>
    </div>
  `;

  output.appendChild(card);

  // Return the container where reviews will be appended
  return card.querySelector(".product-details") as HTMLElement;
};

/**
 * Renders the sales report summary at the end of the dashboard.
 */
const renderSalesReport = (report: {
  totalSales: number;
  unitsSold: number;
  averagePrice: number;
}) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

/**
 * Renders a general error block in red.
 */
const renderError = (message: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = message;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

/**
 * Main async function to orchestrate data fetching, rendering, and error handling.
 */
const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);

    for (const product of products) {
      const productCard = renderProductCard(product);

      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);

        if (reviews.length === 0) {
          renderReview(productCard, "No reviews yet.");
        } else {
          reviews.forEach((review) => {
            renderReview(productCard, `💬 ${review.user}: ${review.comment}`);
          });
        }
      } catch (err) {
        renderReview(productCard, `⚠️ Error loading reviews: ${err}`, "error");
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(`Error fetching sales report: ${err}`);
    }
  } catch (err) {
    renderError(`Fatal Error: ${err}`);
  }
};

// 🔁 Start the app
main();
```

---

### ✅ What This Version Supports
- Product cards with images
- Dynamic reviews under each product
- A sales summary section
- Clean error handling and retry logic
- Clear inline comments for educational purposes

```ts
// src/apiSimulator.ts

// ✅ Define a reusable Product type
export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
  image: string;
}

// ✅ Simulate fetching a product catalog
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          {
            id: 1,
            name: "Laptop",
            price: 1200,
            image: "/assets/laptop2.png"
          },
          {
            id: 2,
            name: "Headphones",
            price: 200,
            image: "/assets/headphone1.png"
          }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

// ✅ Simulate fetching reviews for a product
export const fetchProductReviews = (productId: number): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`);
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

// ✅ Simulate fetching a sales report
export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{ totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({
          totalSales: 50000,
          unitsSold: 250,
          averagePrice: 200
        });
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch sales report");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

ASSISTANT:
Your provided `apiSimulator.ts` is clean, correct, and aligns perfectly with TypeScript and Parcel best practices.

✅ Here's the **final reviewed and approved version** — ready for copy-paste and commit:

```ts
// src/apiSimulator.ts

/**
 * Type definition for Product used across the frontend
 */
export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
  image: string; // Relative path to product image in /public/assets/
}

/**
 * Simulate fetching a product catalog with product details including image path.
 */
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          {
            id: 1,
            name: "Laptop",
            price: 1200,
            image: "/assets/laptop2.jpg"
          },
          {
            id: 2,
            name: "Headphones",
            price: 200,
            image: "/assets/headphone1.jpg"
          }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

/**
 * Simulate fetching user reviews for a given product ID.
 */
export const fetchProductReviews = (productId: number): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`);
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

/**
 * Simulate retrieving a sales report summary.
 */
export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{ totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({
          totalSales: 50000,
          unitsSold: 250,
          averagePrice: 200
        });
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch sales report");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

```ts
// src/apiSimulator.ts

// Import local images (Parcel will handle bundling and URL resolution)
import laptopImg from './assets/laptop2.jpg';
import headphoneImg from './assets/headphone1.jpg';

// Define the Product type used across the app
export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
  image: string;
}

// Simulate fetching a product catalog
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          {
            id: 1,
            name: "Laptop",
            price: 1200,
            image: laptopImg, // ✅ uses imported image
          },
          {
            id: 2,
            name: "Headphones",
            price: 200,
            image: headphoneImg, // ✅ uses imported image
          }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

// Simulate fetching product reviews
export const fetchProductReviews = (productId: number): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`);
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

// Simulate fetching sales report
export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{ totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({
          totalSales: 50000,
          unitsSold: 250,
          averagePrice: 200
        });
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch sales report");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

USER:
before rebiod explain why are you creating the global.d.ts?\

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
Excellent question — this is a key learning moment for understanding how TypeScript and bundlers like **Parcel** work with non-code assets (like images).

---

### 🧠 Why Do We Create `global.d.ts`?

In TypeScript, when you write this:

```ts
import laptopImg from './assets/laptop2.jpg';
```

You're importing a **non-TypeScript module** (a `.jpg` file).

TypeScript **doesn't know what `.jpg` means** unless you tell it.

So if you don’t declare it, TypeScript will throw this error:

```
Cannot find module './assets/laptop2.jpg' or its corresponding type declarations.
```

---

### ✅ The Fix: Declare Module Types for Images

By creating this file:

```ts
// src/global.d.ts
declare module '*.jpg' {
  const value: string;
  export default value;
}
```

You're telling TypeScript:
> "Hey, every time you see a `.jpg` import, treat it as a string URL."

Parcel will handle the actual image loading behind the scenes, and TypeScript will no longer complain.

---

### 💡 Why `global.d.ts`?

- It's a **global declaration file** — TypeScript automatically picks it up
- You can also use `*.d.ts` in `types/` folders or `@types/...` packages for larger apps

---

### 🧼 Summary

| Question                          | Answer                                     |
|----------------------------------|--------------------------------------------|
| Why is `global.d.ts` needed?     | To tell TypeScript how to handle `.jpg` files |
| What does it declare?            | That a `.jpg` module exports a `string`    |
| What happens without it?         | TypeScript error: "Cannot find module ..." |

---

Let me know if you’d like me to add `.png` and `.webp` types too — or if you're ready to rebuild and test image loading.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

USER:
lets add .png and .webp so it indistintly upload them

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
Perfect — great foresight!

Here’s the updated `global.d.ts` that supports `.jpg`, `.jpeg`, `.png`, and `.webp` files. This ensures your project won’t break regardless of which format you use.

---

### ✅ Final `src/global.d.ts`

```ts
declare module '*.jpg' {
  const value: string;
  export default value;
}

declare module '*.jpeg' {
  const value: string;
  export default value;
}

declare module '*.png' {
  const value: string;
  export default value;
}

declare module '*.webp' {
  const value: string;
  export default value;
}
```

---

### 🧠 How This Works

- These are **ambient module declarations**
- Each one says: “when you import a file ending in `.jpg` (or `.png`, etc.), it’s just a string”
- Parcel transforms it into a **URL string** during build time
- TypeScript accepts it thanks to this `.d.ts` file

---

Once added, you’re safe to:
- Rename or swap product images as `.png` or `.webp` without needing code changes
- Import and use images in components, cards, or dynamic loaders

ASSISTANT:
Great catch — based on everything you've shown, it looks like **you've been running the dev server** (`npm run dev`), but **haven’t yet done a full production build**.

---

### ✅ Difference Between `dev` and `build`

| Command          | Purpose                              |
|------------------|--------------------------------------|
| `npm run dev`    | Starts Parcel in **development mode** |
| `npm run build`  | Generates **production-ready static files** (HTML/CSS/JS/images in `dist/`) |

---

### ⚠️ Why This Matters for Images

In **dev mode**, Parcel uses an in-memory server. If images aren’t correctly imported (i.e., via `import`), they’re not served.

When you run `npm run build`:
- Parcel rewrites image references
- It **copies** the image files to `dist/`
- And updates paths like `/assets/laptop2.jpg` → `dist/laptop2.abcd123.jpg`

---

### ✅ Let’s Do It

Run the following:

```bash

npm run build
```

```bash

open dist/index.html    # macOS
xdg-open dist/index.html  # Linux
```

This will show you exactly what the final site will look like when deployed.

ASSISTANT:
Thanks — if the site **isn't showing after the `npm run build`** and opening `dist/index.html`, you're running into a very common Parcel caveat:

---

### 🚫 Problem: `dist/index.html` Doesn't Load Properly

#### Why?

Parcel v2+ rewrites internal asset paths (like JavaScript, CSS, and images) with hashed names like:

```
<script src="/index.abc123.js"></script>
```

These absolute paths (starting with `/`) work on **dev server (`localhost`)**, but **fail when opened directly from disk (file://)**.

---

### ✅ Solutions

#### ✅ Option 1: Test With a Local Web Server (Recommended)

Parcel-built files **must** be tested with a local server:

Run this from your project root:

```bash
npx serve dist
```

Then open the local URL (e.g., `http://localhost:3000`) and everything will work correctly — including images.

---

#### ✅ Option 2:

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
Thanks for the detailed capture — it confirms the issue perfectly.

---

### 🧠 What's Going On?

Your `dist/index.html` contains:

```html
<script type="module" src="/public.ede0f2d2.js"></script>
```

That path (`/public.ede0f2d2.js`) is **absolute** — it assumes the site is served from the root (`/`). But when opening `dist/index.html` **via file://**, this breaks because there's no HTTP server resolving `/`.

---

### ✅ Solution: Serve With a Local Server

To fix this and test your build properly:

#### ✅ 1. Install `serve` (only once)

```bash
npm install -g serve
```

#### ✅ 2. Run it from the root

```bash
serve dist
```

Parcel will serve `dist/index.html` at something like:

```
http://localhost:3000
```

Now everything — including scripts, styles, and images — will work correctly ✅

---

### 🧪 Why Not Just Open From File?

Parcel's output uses **hashed filenames and absolute paths**, which break under `file://` protocol. This is why **opening `dist/index.html` directly from disk never works reliably**.

USER:
chek this first, uploading frontend.ts : // src/frontend.ts
import {
  fetchProductCatalog,
  fetchProductReviews,
  fetchSalesReport,
  Product, // ✅ Import the Product type
} from "./apiSimulator";
import { retryPromise } from "./retryPromise";

// Grab the output container
const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

/**
 * Renders an individual review inside the appropriate product card.
 */
const renderReview = (
  productDetailsDiv: HTMLElement,
  reviewText: string,
  className: string = "review"
) => {
  const reviewDiv = document.createElement("div");
  reviewDiv.className = className;
  reviewDiv.textContent = reviewText;
  productDetailsDiv.appendChild(reviewDiv);
};

/**
 * Renders a complete product card including image, name, price, and review section.
 */
const renderProductCard = (product: Product): HTMLElement => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";

  card.innerHTML = `
    <div class="card-content">
      <img src="${product.image}" alt="${product.name}" class="product-image" />
      <div class="product-details">
        <h2>${product.name}</h2>
        <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
        <h3>Reviews:</h3>
      </div>
    </div>
  `;

  output.appendChild(card);

  // Return the container where reviews will be appended
  return card.querySelector(".product-details") as HTMLElement;
};

/**
 * Renders the sales report summary at the end of the dashboard.
 */
const renderSalesReport = (report: {
  totalSales: number;
  unitsSold: number;
  averagePrice: number;
}) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

/**
 * Renders a general error block in red.
 */
const renderError = (message: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = message;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

/**
 * Main async function to orchestrate data fetching, rendering, and error handling.
 */
const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);

    for (const product of products) {
      const productCard = renderProductCard(product);

      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);

        if (reviews.length === 0) {
          renderReview(productCard, "No reviews yet.");
        } else {
          reviews.forEach((review) => {
            renderReview(productCard, `💬 ${review.user}: ${review.comment}`);
          });
        }
      } catch (err) {
        renderReview(productCard, `⚠️ Error loading reviews: ${err}`, "error");
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(`Error fetching sales report: ${err}`);
    }
  } catch (err) {
    renderError(`Fatal Error: ${err}`);
  }
};

// 🔁 Start the app
main();

### ✅ `src/apiSimulator.ts`

```ts
// src/apiSimulator.ts

// 🔰 Correctly import image assets (Parcel will hash these)
import laptopImg from "../public/assets/laptop2.jpg";
import headphoneImg from "../public/assets/headphone1.jpg";

// ✅ Define a reusable Product type
export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
  image: string; // 🔹 This should be a string URL
}

// ✅ Simulate fetching a product catalog
```

ASSISTANT:
Thanks for the screenshot — the issue is now completely clear.

---

### 🧠 Root Cause
Your import path in `apiSimulator.ts`:

```ts
import laptopImg from "../public/assets/laptop2.jpg";
```

is incorrect because:

- The `public/` folder **is not part of the module resolution scope** for TypeScript/Parcel import paths.
- Parcel handles `public/` **as root-relative** for runtime (e.g. `<img src="/assets/laptop2.jpg">`), **but not** for static `import` statements.

---

### ✅ Correct Fix

Move the images **from `public/assets/` into `src/assets/`**, then update the import like this:

```ts
import laptopImg from "./assets/laptop2.jpg";
import headphoneImg from "./assets/headphone1.jpg";
```

Here's how your project structure should look after the move:

```
ecommerce_dashboard_frontend/

│   │   ├── laptop2.jpg
│   │   ├── headphone1.jpg
│   ├── apiSimulator.ts
│   ├── frontend.ts
│   └── ...
├── public/
│   └── index.html
```

Then rebuild:

```bash
rm -rf .parcel-cache dist
npm run build
npx serve dist
```

ASSISTANT:
Thanks for your patience! From your screenshots and setup, everything seems correctly structured. However, the **product images are still not showing** due to how **Parcel handles asset imports**.

### 🔍 Root Cause
You're referencing images like:

```ts
image: "/assets/laptop2.jpg"
```

…but **Parcel doesn't copy unreferenced assets in `/public/assets` unless directly imported in the source code**. So these static paths fail silently because they’re not bundled.

---

### ✅ The Solution

To make it work consistently with Parcel, **you must import images in your TypeScript source** using ES module imports, like this:

---

```ts
            id: 2,
            name: "Headphones",
```

USER:
in one import you put .. / and in other . / which one is correct in this case?

ASSISTANT:
Great catch!

In your case, **`../public/assets/...` is incorrect** because you're importing from `src/`, and `public/` is **not** part of the importable TypeScript module path during bundling with Parcel.

### ✅ Correct usage:
Since `assets/` is **inside `src/`**, and you're importing from a file like `src/apiSimulator.ts`, you should use:

```ts
import laptopImg from "./assets/laptop2.jpg";
import headphoneImg from "./assets/headphone1.jpg";
```

### Why?
- `.` refers to the **current folder**, which is `src/`.
- `./assets/...` correctly resolves to `src/assets/...`.

### ❌ What’s wrong with `../public/assets/...`?
- Parcel doesn’t allow importing from `public/` like that.
- `public/` is meant for static assets referenced in HTML, not via `import` in TS/JS.
- You **cannot** use `import ... from '../public/...'` for bundling image modules.

---

### ✅ Final Fix
Update your import statements to:

```ts
import laptopImg from "./assets/laptop2.jpg";
import headphoneImg from "./assets/headphone1.jpg";
```

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
Thanks for the clear screenshot — you're very close. Here’s the root issue based on what I see in the `dist/` folder and generated `index.html`:

---

### 🧠 What’s Happening

Your `index.html` has the following import map:
```html
<script type="importmap">
{
  "imports": {
    "2CcHI": "/laptop2.f7038046.jpg",
    "jwTbI": "/headphone1.8f201a6a.jpg"
  }
}
</script>
```

But you're **not actually using those import aliases** (`2CcHI`, `jwTbI`) in your **JavaScript or TypeScript code**.

So **the images are being bundled and hashed correctly**, but you’re not telling Parcel to inject them properly into the DOM.

---

### ✅ Proper Fix Strategy

You need to **import the images as modules** inside your TypeScript like this:

```ts
import laptopImg from "./assets/laptop2.jpg";
import headphoneImg from "./assets/headphone1.jpg";
```

Then in your product object:

```ts
resolve([
  {
    id: 1,
    name: "Laptop",
    price: 1200,
    image: laptopImg  // ✅ uses imported module
  },
  {
    id: 2,
    name: "Headphones",
    price: 200,
    image: headphoneImg  // ✅ uses imported module
  }
])
```

Parcel will now rewrite the image paths into those hashed names **automatically**.

---

### 🚫 What NOT to Do

Do NOT write paths like this manually:

```ts
image: "/assets/laptop2.jpg"  // ❌ won't be resolved after bundling
```

That causes the browser to look for `/assets/laptop2.jpg`, which doesn’t exist in the `dist` root (only the hashed version does).

---

### ✅ Next Steps

1. Make sure your product image paths are imported like above.
2. Reference those variables in your `image:` field.
3. Run `npm run build`.
4. Open `dist/index.html` via `npx serve dist` and the images will now show.

ASSISTANT:
The errors you’re seeing — `Failed to load resource: the server responded with a status of 404 (Not Found)` pointing to `[object%20Object]` — strongly indicate that the **image path isn't being correctly resolved or passed** during runtime.

This is a classic issue that happens when a non-string value (like an imported asset handled by Parcel) is not being used properly in your rendering code.

---

### ✅ Here's what to do now to **fix it cleanly**:

Let’s make **absolutely sure** that:
1. Parcel handles the image as a URL.
2. We are not serializing or embedding an object unintentionally.

---

### 🔧 Fix: Ensure the `image` property is being rendered as a `string`

In `frontend.ts`, you may be using a `Product` type where `image` is actually being set to an object (the import) but then treated like a string improperly.

Update your `renderProductCard` function like so:

```ts
const renderProductCard = (product: Product): HTMLElement => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";

  // ✅ Ensure product.image is treated as a string URL
  const imageUrl = typeof product.image === "string" ? product.image : String(product.image);

  card.innerHTML = `
    <div class="card-content">
      <img src="${imageUrl}" alt="${product.name}" class="product-image" />
      <div class="product-details">
        <h2>${product.name}</h2>
        <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
        <h3>Reviews:</h3>
      </div>
    </div>
  `;

  output.appendChild(card);
  return card.querySelector(".product-details") as HTMLElement;
};
```

---

### ✅ Why this works

When Parcel processes images via `import laptop from "./img.jpg"`, it actually **replaces** the import with a URL **string** pointing to the file in `dist`. However, if that value is not interpolated properly into HTML or ends up being serialized (e.g. via `JSON.stringify` or passed as a raw object), it shows as `[object Object]` — exactly what your error log shows.

---

Let me know once you update that function so we can test again.

  // ✅ Ensure product.image is treated as a string URL

  card.innerHTML = `
    <div class="card-content">
      <img src="${imageUrl}" alt="${product.name}" class="product-image" />
      <div class="product-details">

  totalSales: number;
  unitsSold: number;
  averagePrice: number;
}) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

/**
 * Renders a general error block in red.
 */
const renderError = (message: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = message;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

/**
 * Main async function to orchestrate data fetching, rendering, and error handling.
 */
const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);

    for (const product of products) {
      const productCard = renderProductCard(product);

      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);

        if (reviews.length === 0) {
          renderReview(productCard, "No reviews yet.");
        } else {
          reviews.forEach((review) => {
            renderReview(productCard, `💬 ${review.user}: ${review.comment}`);
          });
        }
      } catch (err) {
        renderReview(productCard, `⚠️ Error loading reviews: ${err}`, "error");
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(`Error fetching sales report: ${err}`);
    }
  } catch (err) {
    renderError(`Fatal Error: ${err}`);
  }
};

// 🔁 Start the app
main();

```ts
  productDetailsDiv: HTMLElement,

  reviewDiv.textContent = reviewText;

  const card = document.createElement("div");

  totalSales: number;

    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

/**
 * ✅ Render a generic error message.

  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = message;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

/**

    for (const product of products) {
      const productCard = renderProductCard(product);

        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);
```

ASSISTANT:
Thanks! Your current `tsconfig.json` is good for **Node.js-style backend development**, but since you're building a **frontend app with Parcel**, we need to adjust a few things to align with **modern frontend bundling practices**.

---

### ✅ Here's the updated and recommended `tsconfig.json` for Parcel + TypeScript + frontend:

```json
{
  "compilerOptions": {
    "target": "ES6",
    "module": "ESNext",
    "moduleResolution": "Bundler",
    "rootDir": "./src",
    "outDir": "./dist",
    "strict": true,
    "esModuleInterop": true,
    "forceConsistentCasingInFileNames": true,
    "skipLibCheck": true
  },
  "include": ["src"]
}
```

---

### 🔍 Key Fixes:
| Option                  | Why It's Important                                          |
|------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------|
| `"module": "ESNext"`   | Enables modern `import`/`export` syntax Parcel supports.   |
| `"moduleResolution": "Bundler"` | Required so Parcel can resolve assets and `.jpg`, `.png` properly. |
| `"include": ["src"]`   | Ensures TypeScript only compiles what's inside `src/`.     |

---

### ✅ Next Steps:
1. Replace your `tsconfig.json` content with the one above.
2. Restart your editor/TS server if needed (`Ctrl+Shift+P > TypeScript: Restart TS Server`).

ASSISTANT:
Great question! Restarting your **editor** or **TypeScript language server** ensures that changes in your `tsconfig.json`, dependencies, or code structure are picked up correctly. This helps fix issues like stale type errors, autocomplete problems, or unexpected import resolution failures.

---

## 🔁 How to Restart TypeScript in Visual Studio Code (VS Code):

### ✅ Option 1: Restart TypeScript Server
1. **Open Command Palette**  
   Press `Ctrl + Shift + P` (or `Cmd + Shift + P` on Mac).

2. **Search** for:  
   ```
   TypeScript: Restart TS Server
   ```

3. **Click it**, and it will restart the internal TypeScript service VS Code uses.

---

### ✅ Option 2: Reload Window (Full Editor Restart)
If things are still stuck or glitchy:

1. Open the Command Palette:  
   `Ctrl + Shift + P` (or `Cmd + Shift + P` on Mac)

2. Search for:  
   ```
   Reload Window
   ```

3. Select it.  
   This will reload VS Code entirely, without quitting it.

---

### ✅ Option 3: Manually Close and Reopen VS Code
You can always just:
- **Close VS Code completely**
- **Reopen it** in your project folder  
This will also restart everything, including the TS Server.

---

### 🛠 When Should You Do This?
- After editing `tsconfig.json`
- After installing or removing packages
- After changing module formats or path aliases
- When autocompletion or IntelliSense is broken

### ⚠️ Final Fix Suggestion for Image Display

```ts

```

…you are assigning a static path string, but **Parcel doesn’t bundle this file into `dist/assets` unless you explicitly import it**.

### ✅ Recommended Fix (Consistent with Parcel Best Practices)

Update `apiSimulator.ts` to import the image modules:

```ts
import laptopImg from "../assets/laptop2.jpg";
import headphoneImg from "../assets/headphone1.jpg";
```

And then use the imported variables:

```ts
image: laptopImg
```

This ensures that Parcel correctly **copies and hashes the files**, and returns their final path.

- All **asset paths must be imported** if referenced dynamically.
- Serve via `npx serve dist` **only after building with `parcel build`**.

USER:
are you to use .. /

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
Great question!

### 📌 Use `../` vs `./` in Imports — What’s Correct?

The correct usage depends entirely on **where your current file is** and **where the target file is located** **relative to it**.

---

### In your case (`src/apiSimulator.ts` ➜ `src/assets/`):

You're importing images from the `src/assets` directory, so:

```ts
// ✅ Correct relative path:
import laptopImg from "./assets/laptop2.jpg";
import headphoneImg from "./assets/headphone1.jpg";
```

### ❌ Why `../assets/` is wrong here:

`../` would try to go **up one directory**, which would resolve to `ecommerce_dashboard_frontend/assets` (outside `src`) — but your assets are **inside** `src/assets`.

---

### ✅ Summary Rule:

- Use `./` to reference something in the same folder.
- Use `./assets/...` to reference something **inside a subfolder** of your current directory.
- Use `../` only if you are going **up one level**.

---

So yes — in your actual `apiSimulator.ts`, you should use:

```ts
import laptopImg from "./assets/laptop2.jpg";
```

Let me know when you're ready, and I’ll help you refactor and test this cleanly.

  ```json
      "module": "ESNext",
      "moduleResolution": "Bundler",
  ```

  This configuration aligns with Parcel's requirements for module resolution and bundling.

  ```ts

  declare module "*.png";
  declare module "*.webp";
  ```
  This informs TypeScript about the imported image modules.

---

### 🔍 Potential Issues and Solutions

Despite the correct setup, images are not displaying. Let's explore possible causes:

#### 1. **Image Files Not Being Bundled**

Ensure that the image files are located within the `src/assets/` directory and are being imported in your code. Parcel only includes assets in the build if they are referenced in the source code.

#### 2. **Incorrect Image Paths in HTML**

If you're referencing images directly in your HTML (e.g., `<img src="/assets/laptop2.jpg" />`), Parcel won't process these unless you use the `require` or `import` statements in your JavaScript/TypeScript code. Ensure all image references are handled via imports.

#### 3. **Development Server vs. Production Build**

Parcel handles asset paths differently in development and production modes. To ensure consistent behavior:

- For development:
  ```bash
  npm run start
  ```
- For production:
  ```bash
  npm run build
  npx serve dist
  ```

Verify that images load correctly in both modes.

#### 4. **Browser Caching Issues**

Sometimes, browsers cache assets aggressively. Try clearing your browser cache or performing a hard refresh (`Ctrl + F5` or `Cmd + Shift + R`) to see if the images load correctly.

---

### 🛠️ Additional Steps

To further diagnose and resolve the issue:

1. **Inspect Network Requests**: Open your browser's developer tools (usually `F12`), go to the Network tab, and reload the page. Check if there are any 404 errors for image files.

2. **Verify Output Directory**: After building the project, inspect the `dist` directory to ensure that the image files are present and correctly hashed.

3. **Check Image URLs**: In the rendered HTML, verify that the `src` attributes of `<img>` tags point to the correct paths. They should match the hashed filenames in the `dist` directory.

---

- [x] Images are imported using `import` statements in TypeScript files.

### **3. Create Simulated API (src/apiSimulator.ts)**

Create three exported functions:
- `fetchProductCatalog`
- `fetchProductReviews`
- `fetchSalesReport`

Also, define the `Product` type and image imports:
```ts
// src/apiSimulator.ts
import laptopImg from "./assets/laptop2.jpg";
import headphoneImg from "./assets/headphone1.jpg";

export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
  image: string;
}

export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve) =>
    setTimeout(() => {
      resolve([
        { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200, image: laptopImg },
        { id: 2, name: "Headphones", price: 200, image: headphoneImg },
      ]);
    }, 1000)
  );
};

export const fetchProductReviews = (
  productId: number
): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> =>
  new Promise((resolve) =>
    setTimeout(() => {
      resolve([
        { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
        { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." },
      ]);
    }, 1000)
  );

export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{
  totalSales: number;
  unitsSold: number;
  averagePrice: number;
}> =>
  new Promise((resolve) =>
    setTimeout(() => {
      resolve({
        totalSales: 50000,
        unitsSold: 250,
        averagePrice: 200,
      });
    }, 1000)
  );
```

---

### ✅ Commit 3: `feat: add simulated API functions with product and review mocks`

---

### **4. Retry Utility (src/retryPromise.ts)**

```ts
export const retryPromise = async <T>(
  fn: () => Promise<T>,
  retries: number,
  delay: number
): Promise<T> => {
  for (let i = 0; i < retries; i++) {
    try {
      return await fn();
    } catch (error) {
      if (i === retries - 1) throw error;
      await new Promise((res) => setTimeout(res, delay));
    }
  }
  throw new Error("Retry failed");
};
```

---

### ✅ Commit 4: `feat: add retry utility to handle transient errors`
