Promises and Error Handling Challenge
Scenario
You are developing an e-commerce dashboard that fetches data from various APIs, including a product catalog, user reviews, and a sales report. Each API call could potentially fail due to network issues, incorrect endpoints, or data inconsistencies. To build a stable and user-friendly application, you need to manage these scenarios with proper error handling.

Task
In this lab, you will build a small application that leverages asynchronous API calls using Promises. You will also implement error handling to ensure that the application can manage unexpected issues gracefully. This lab will test your ability to work with asynchronous programming concepts, as well as to manage errors effectively in a real-world scenario.

Objectives
By the end of this lab, you will be able to:

Apply Promises to manage multiple asynchronous operations in JavaScript.
Implement chained Promises to handle sequential data retrieval and manage dependencies between API calls.
Utilize .catch() and .finally() to handle errors and perform cleanup tasks in a Promise chain.
Design custom error classes to improve error identification and debugging.
Implement a retry mechanism to manage failed asynchronous requests, enhancing application resilience.
Analyze the benefits and challenges of using error handling strategies in complex asynchronous workflows.

### ✅ **Step 2: Implement API Simulation Functions**

We'll now implement the mock API functions in `src/apiSimulator.ts`. These simulate network calls and introduce controlled failures for testing our error handling.

---

### 📄 `src/apiSimulator.ts`

```ts
// Define a Product type for strong typing
export type Product = {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
};

// Simulate fetching a product catalog
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200 },
          { id: 2, name: "Headphones", price: 200 },
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

// Simulate fetching reviews for a product
export const fetchProductReviews = (productId: number): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`);
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

// Simulate fetching a sales report
export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{ totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({
          totalSales: 50000,
          unitsSold: 250,
          averagePrice: 200
        });
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch sales report");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

### ✅ **Step 3: Build the Main Application Logic**

Now we’ll create `index.ts`, which will coordinate our API calls, apply error handling, and log results.

---

### 📄 `src/index.ts`

```ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from "./apiSimulator";

// Entry point function
const runDashboard = () => {
  // Step 1: Fetch product catalog
  fetchProductCatalog()
    .then(products => {
      console.log("✅ Products:", products);

      // Step 2: Fetch reviews for each product
      const reviewPromises = products.map(product =>
        fetchProductReviews(product.id)
          .then(reviews => {
            console.log(`💬 Reviews for ${product.name}:`, reviews);
          })
          .catch(err => {
            console.error(`⚠️ Error fetching reviews for ${product.name}:`, err);
          })
      );

      // Step 3: After all reviews, fetch sales report
      Promise.all(reviewPromises)
        .then(() => {
          return fetchSalesReport();
        })
        .then(report => {
          console.log("📊 Sales Report:", report);
        })
        .catch(err => {
          console.error("⚠️ Error fetching sales report:", err);
        })
        .finally(() => {
          console.log("✅ All API calls attempted.");
        });
    })
    .catch(err => {
      console.error("❌ Fatal error fetching product catalog:", err);
    });
};

runDashboard();
```

### ✅ **Step 4: Add Custom Error Classes**

This step improves error categorization and makes debugging more effective.

### 📄 `src/errors.ts`

```ts
// Custom error for network-related issues
export class NetworkError extends Error {
  constructor(message: string) {
    super(message);
    this.name = "NetworkError";
  }
}

// Custom error for data inconsistencies or missing fields
export class DataError extends Error {
  constructor(message: string) {
    super(message);
    this.name = "DataError";
  }
}
```

---

### 🔧 Update `apiSimulator.ts` to use these classes

Replace all basic `reject("...")` with these custom classes:

```ts
import { NetworkError, DataError } from "./errors";

// Example update inside fetchProductCatalog
if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
  resolve([...]);
} else {
  reject(new NetworkError("Failed to fetch product catalog"));
}
```

Make similar updates in:
- `fetchProductReviews`

### 📄 `src/apiSimulator.ts`

```ts
import { NetworkError, DataError } from "./errors";

export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
}

// ✅ Simulate fetching a product catalog
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200 },
          { id: 2, name: "Headphones", price: 200 },
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(new NetworkError("Failed to fetch product catalog"));
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

// ✅ Simulate fetching reviews for a product
export const fetchProductReviews = (productId: number): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(new NetworkError(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`));
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

// ✅ Simulate fetching a sales report
export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{ totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({
          totalSales: 50000,
          unitsSold: 250,
          averagePrice: 200
        });
      } else {
        reject(new DataError("Failed to fetch sales report"));
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

ASSISTANT:
Great! To test the updated `apiSimulator.ts` with custom error handling, we’ll proceed in the following steps:

---

### ✅ 1. **Create a Test Entry Point (`index.ts`)**

This file will simulate calling all your API functions, and handle errors using `try/catch`. Here's a simple version for testing:

```ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from './apiSimulator';
import { NetworkError, DataError } from './errors';

const testAPI = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await fetchProductCatalog();
    console.log("✅ Product Catalog:", products);

    for (const product of products) {
      try {
        const reviews = await fetchProductReviews(product.id);
        console.log(`✅ Reviews for ${product.name}:`, reviews);
      } catch (error) {
        if (error instanceof NetworkError) {
          console.error("🌐 Network error fetching reviews:", error.message);
        } else {
          console.error("⚠️ Unexpected error fetching reviews:", error);
        }
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await fetchSalesReport();
      console.log("✅ Sales Report:", report);
    } catch (error) {
      if (error instanceof DataError) {
        console.error("📊 Data error fetching sales report:", error.message);
      } else {
        console.error("⚠️ Unexpected error fetching sales report:", error);
      }
    }

  } catch (error) {
    if (error instanceof NetworkError) {
      console.error("🌐 Network error fetching catalog:", error.message);
    } else {
      console.error("❌ Unexpected fatal error:", error);
    }
  }
};

testAPI();
```

```ts
// Represents a network-related error (e.g., connection issues, timeouts)
export class NetworkError extends Error {
  constructor(message: string) {
    super(message);
    this.name = "NetworkError";
  }
}

// Represents a data-related error (e.g., missing fields, invalid response)
export class DataError extends Error {
  constructor(message: string) {
    super(message);
    this.name = "DataError";
  }
}
```

### 🔁 Step: Update `src/apiSimulator.ts`

Here is the full **refactored** version of the file using the custom errors. **Replace your existing file content** with this:

```ts
// src/apiSimulator.ts

import { NetworkError, DataError } from "./customErrors";

// Define a reusable Product type
export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
}

// Simulate fetching a product catalog
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200 },
          { id: 2, name: "Headphones", price: 200 },
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(new NetworkError("Failed to fetch product catalog"));
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

// Simulate fetching reviews for a product
export const fetchProductReviews = (productId: number): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(new NetworkError(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`));
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

// Simulate fetching a sales report
export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{ totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({
          totalSales: 50000,
          unitsSold: 250,
          averagePrice: 200
        });
      } else {
        reject(new DataError("Failed to fetch sales report"));
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

---

### 🧠 Why It Matters

Using `NetworkError` and `DataError` allows you to identify and handle different failure types more intelligently in your logic later — ideal for retry strategies or UI feedback.

### 🧱 Step: Create `retryPromise.ts`

This utility will retry a failed async function up to a given number of times with a delay.

Create the file:

```bash
touch src/retryPromise.ts
```

---

### 🧾 File: `src/retryPromise.ts`

Paste this code:

```ts
// src/retryPromise.ts

/**
 * Retries an async operation on failure.
 *
 * @param fn - A function that returns a Promise
 * @param retries - Number of retry attempts
 * @param delay - Delay between retries in milliseconds
 */
export const retryPromise = async <T>(
  fn: () => Promise<T>,
  retries: number,
  delay: number
): Promise<T> => {
  try {
    return await fn();
  } catch (error) {
    if (retries > 0) {
      console.warn(`Retrying... Attempts left: ${retries}`);
      await new Promise(res => setTimeout(res, delay));
      return retryPromise(fn, retries - 1, delay);
    } else {
      throw error;
    }
  }
};
```

---

Once created, let’s commit it. After that, we’ll update `index.ts` to use `retryPromise`. Let me know when ready.

### 🧾 Update: `src/index.ts`

Replace the existing contents of `index.ts` with the following:

```ts
// src/index.ts
import {
  fetchProductCatalog,
  fetchProductReviews,
  fetchSalesReport,
} from "./apiSimulator";
import { retryPromise } from "./retryPromise";
import { NetworkError, DataError } from "./customErrors";

// ✅ Helper to log results or errors
const log = (label: string, data: any) => {
  console.log(`✅ ${label}:`, data);
};

// ✅ Helper to log errors
const logError = (label: string, error: any) => {
  if (error instanceof NetworkError) {
    console.error(`🌐 Network error ${label}:`, error.message);
  } else if (error instanceof DataError) {
    console.error(`📊 Data error ${label}:`, error.message);
  } else {
    console.error(`❌ Unknown error ${label}:`, error);
  }
};

// ✅ Main async workflow using retry
const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);
    log("Product Catalog", products);

    for (const product of products) {
      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);
        log(`Reviews for ${product.name}`, reviews);
      } catch (err) {
        logError(`fetching reviews for ${product.name}`, err);
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      log("Sales Report", report);
    } catch (err) {
      logError("fetching sales report", err);
    }

  } catch (err) {
    logError("overall application", err);
  }
};

// 🔁 Run the app
main();
```

---

This version:
- Uses `retryPromise` for all fetches.
- Differentiates between network and data errors using your custom error classes.

## 3️⃣ Code Overview

### `apiSimulator.ts`

- **Simulates API behavior** for fetching product catalog, reviews, and sales report.
- Uses `Math.random()` to occasionally fail and simulate real-world API flakiness.
- Rejects Promises using `NetworkError` or `DataError` custom classes.

### `retryPromise.ts`

- Implements a generic retry mechanism using recursion.
- Retries failed API calls up to 3 times, with a delay between each.

### `customErrors.ts`

- Defines `NetworkError` and `DataError` to enhance clarity in error logs and debugging.

### `index.ts`

- Main entry point: orchestrates all API calls.
- Logs successful data or appropriate error messages using `try/catch`.
- Demonstrates use of custom error classes and retry logic.

```bash

✅ Sales Report: {...}
```

---

## 5️⃣ Educational Concepts

### 🔁 Promises

- Model asynchronous operations (like API calls)
- Support chaining with `.then()` and `.catch()`

### ❌ Error Handling

- Each API is wrapped in `try/catch` to isolate and manage individual failures.

### 🧠 Custom Errors

- `NetworkError`: Indicates connectivity issues.
- `DataError`: Flags invalid data structures.

### 🔄 Retry Logic

- Automatically retries failed Promises up to 3 times.
- Uses recursion and `setTimeout` for controlled retries.

### 📘 `TUTORIAL.md` — E-Commerce Dashboard: Backend Development Walkthrough

---

## 🎯 Objective

Build a robust backend simulation for an **e-commerce dashboard** using TypeScript. Learn how to handle **asynchronous operations**, simulate **API unreliability**, and build **resilient workflows** using Promises, custom errors, and retry logic.

---

## 🗂️ Project Setup

```bash
mkdir e-commerce-dashboard
cd e-commerce-dashboard
npm init -y
npm install typescript @types/node --save-dev
npx tsc --init
```

### 🔧 Sample `tsconfig.json`:

```json
{
  "compilerOptions": {
    "target": "ES6",
    "module": "CommonJS",
    "rootDir": "./src",
    "outDir": "./dist",
    "strict": true,
    "esModuleInterop": true
  }
}
```

---

## 📁 Project Structure

```
e-commerce-dashboard/
│
├── src/
│   ├── apiSimulator.ts        # Simulates API calls
│   ├── retryPromise.ts        # Implements retry mechanism
│   ├── customErrors.ts        # Custom error classes
│   ├── index.ts               # Main application logic
│
├── dist/
├── package.json
├── tsconfig.json
├── README.md
├── TUTORIAL.md
```

---

## 💡 Core Concepts & Implementation

### 1️⃣ Promises – Asynchronous Workflows

#### Example (in `apiSimulator.ts`):
```ts
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      Math.random() < 0.8
        ? resolve([{ id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200 }])
        : reject(new NetworkError("Failed to fetch product catalog"));
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

**💬 Why?** Simulates a network call that might fail — gives a realistic feel of working with APIs.

---

### 2️⃣ Custom Errors – Improve Debugging

#### In `customErrors.ts`:
```ts
export class NetworkError extends Error {
  constructor(message: string) {
    super(message);
    this.name = "NetworkError";
  }
}
```

**💬 Why?** Differentiates between a network problem and a bad data structure — great for troubleshooting and logging.

---

### 3️⃣ Retry Mechanism – Resilient Operations

#### In `retryPromise.ts`:
```ts
export const retryPromise = async <T>(
  fn: () => Promise<T>,
  retries: number,
  delay: number
): Promise<T> => {
  try {
    return await fn();
  } catch (error) {
    if (retries <= 1) throw error;
    console.log(`Retrying... Attempts left: ${retries - 1}`);
    await new Promise((res) => setTimeout(res, delay));
    return retryPromise(fn, retries - 1, delay);
  }
};
```

**💬 Why?** A failing API call gets additional chances to succeed — improves reliability in flaky conditions.

---

### 4️⃣ Main Application Logic – Orchestrating Calls

#### In `index.ts`:
```ts
const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);

for (const product of products) {
  try {
    const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);
    console.log(`✅ Reviews for ${product.name}:`, reviews);
  } catch (err) {
    console.error(`🌐 Network error fetching reviews: ${err}`);
  }
}
```

**💬 Why?** Demonstrates chaining, retry logic, and precise error handling at a product level.

---

## 🚀 Run & Test

```bash
npm run build
npm start
```

## 🧩 How It All Connects

| Concept        | Role                                                  | Related File         |
|----------------|--------------------------------------------------------|----------------------|
| Promises       | Model async API calls                                  | `apiSimulator.ts`    |
| Custom Errors  | Distinguish error types                                | `customErrors.ts`    |
| Retry Logic    | Handle transient failures automatically                | `retryPromise.ts`    |
| Main Logic     | Glues everything together with precise error reporting | `index.ts`           |

## 🧠 Practice Questions

1. What are the advantages of handling errors locally within each async operation?
2. How do `NetworkError` and `DataError` improve your debugging workflow?
3. Why is it valuable to retry a failed request instead of immediately failing?

### 🛠 Explanation of the Scripts

- **`build`**: Runs the TypeScript compiler (`tsc`) for backend and bundles frontend with Parcel.
- **`dev`**: Launches Parcel’s dev server at `http://localhost:1234`, ideal for real-time frontend updates.
- **`start`**: Runs your Node.js backend from the compiled `dist/index.js`.

ASSISTANT:
Great! Here's how we'll **progressively integrate your backend logic into the working Parcel-based frontend**, with explanations at each step.

---

## 🧠 **Goal Recap**
You already have backend logic (`fetchProductCatalog`, `fetchProductReviews`, `fetchSalesReport`, and `retryPromise`) in `src/` (TypeScript files). Now we'll use that logic in the frontend (in `frontend-parcel/`) to display the data visually.

---

## ✅ **Step 1: Move or Reuse Backend Logic**

**Why:** Parcel only builds from within the `frontend-parcel/` folder right now. But your logic lives in `src/`.

**Options:**
- 🔁 **Copy** only the reusable logic into the frontend (best for separation).
- 🔗 Or **restructure the project** later to unify both.

### ✅ Action:
Create this new file:

📄 `frontend-parcel/apiSimulator.ts`

Paste in the following mock backend logic:

```ts
export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
}

export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200 },
          { id: 2, name: "Headphones", price: 200 },
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

export const fetchProductReviews = (productId: number): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`);
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{ totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({
          totalSales: 50000,
          unitsSold: 250,
          averagePrice: 200
        });
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch sales report");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

---

## ✅ **Step 2: Import the Logic and Display Product Data**

Open `frontend-parcel/main.ts` and replace its content with:

```ts
import { fetchProductCatalog } from "./apiSimulator";

const output = document.getElementById("output")!;
output.textContent = "Loading products...";

fetchProductCatalog()
  .then((products) => {
    output.innerHTML = "<h2>Product Catalog</h2>";
    products.forEach((product) => {
      const div = document.createElement("div");
      div.className = "card";
      div.innerHTML = `<strong>${product.name}</strong> - $${product.price}`;
      output.appendChild(div);
    });
  })
  .catch((error) => {
    output.innerHTML = `<span style="color:red;">Error: ${error}</span>`;
  });
```

### Explanation:
- `import`: brings in your backend function.
- `output.innerHTML`: replaces "Loading..." with product details.
- `.catch()`: handles errors in a user-friendly way.

```ts
if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
  resolve([...]);
} else {
  reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
```

#### 🔧 Step-by-Step Plan:

1. **Update `main.ts`** to:
   - Import `retryPromise`.
   - Use `retryPromise()` with `fetchProductCatalog`, `fetchProductReviews`, and `fetchSalesReport`.

2. **Ensure UI behavior:**
   - Show a loading state.
   - Replace it with products or error messages after retries.

---

### 📄 Updated `main.ts` (with Retry Logic)

```ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from "../src/apiSimulator";
import { retryPromise } from "../src/retryPromise";

const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

const renderError = (message: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = `Error: ${message}`;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

const renderProduct = (product: { id: number; name: string; price: number }) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>${product.name}</h2>
    <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
    <div id="reviews-${product.id}">Loading reviews...</div>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

const renderReview = (productId: number, reviews: { user: string; comment: string }[]) => {
  const container = document.getElementById(`reviews-${productId}`)!;
  container.innerHTML = `<h3>Reviews:</h3>`;
  reviews.forEach((r) => {
    const p = document.createElement("p");
    p.textContent = `💬 ${r.user}: ${r.comment}`;
    container.appendChild(p);
  });
};

const renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

const main = async () => {
  output.innerHTML = "Loading...";

  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);
    output.innerHTML = "";

    for (const product of products) {
      renderProduct(product);

      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);
        renderReview(product.id, reviews);
      } catch (err) {
        renderError(`Reviews for ${product.name}: ${err}`);
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(`Sales report: ${err}`);
    }
  } catch (err) {
    output.innerHTML = "";
    renderError(`Failed to fetch product catalog: ${err}`);
  }
};

main();
```

```
feat(frontend): integrate retry mechanism in UI logic for all API calls
```

- Good for totally different direction or if collaborating with others.
- But syncing changes between fork and original can get messy.

🔁 Better suited for **collaborative or public projects**.

### ✅ Step 1: Render Product Reviews

### 🔧 Update `frontend-parcel/main.ts`

Here’s the updated file with **educational comments**:

```ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from "../src/apiSimulator";

// 1. Reference the HTML element where we will inject our UI
const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

// 2. A function to create a card per product
const renderProductCard = (product: { id: number; name: string; price: number }) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>${product.name}</h2>
    <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
    <div class="reviews" id="reviews-${product.id}">Loading reviews...</div>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

// 3. A function to update the product card with fetched reviews
const appendReviews = (productId: number, reviews: { user: string; comment: string }[]) => {
  const reviewsDiv = document.getElementById(`reviews-${productId}`)!;
  reviewsDiv.innerHTML = "<h3>Reviews:</h3>";
  reviews.forEach((review) => {
    const p = document.createElement("p");
    p.className = "review";
    p.textContent = `💬 ${review.user}: ${review.comment}`;
    reviewsDiv.appendChild(p);
  });
};

// 4. Main app function: fetch products and their reviews
const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await fetchProductCatalog();
    products.forEach(async (product) => {
      renderProductCard(product);
      try {
        const reviews = await fetchProductReviews(product.id);
        appendReviews(product.id, reviews);
      } catch (error) {
        const reviewsDiv = document.getElementById(`reviews-${product.id}`)!;
        reviewsDiv.innerHTML = `<p class="error">⚠️ Error loading reviews: ${error}</p>`;
      }
    });
  } catch (error) {
    output.innerHTML = `<p class="error">Fatal Error: ${error}</p>`;
  }
};

main();
```

### 🔧 Update `frontend-parcel/main.ts`

Below is your updated `main.ts` file with the **sales report logic** added:

```ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from "../src/apiSimulator";

// Output container for UI
const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

/**
 * Create and display a product card
 */
const renderProductCard = (product: { id: number; name: string; price: number }) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>${product.name}</h2>
    <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
    <div class="reviews" id="reviews-${product.id}">Loading reviews...</div>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

/**
 * Append fetched reviews into a product card
 */
const appendReviews = (productId: number, reviews: { user: string; comment: string }[]) => {
  const reviewsDiv = document.getElementById(`reviews-${productId}`)!;
  reviewsDiv.innerHTML = "<h3>Reviews:</h3>";
  reviews.forEach((review) => {
    const p = document.createElement("p");
    p.className = "review";
    p.textContent = `💬 ${review.user}: ${review.comment}`;
    reviewsDiv.appendChild(p);
  });
};

/**
 * Show a summarized sales report at the bottom
 */
const renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "card";
  div.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

// Main application logic
const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await fetchProductCatalog();
    products.forEach(async (product) => {
      renderProductCard(product);
      try {
        const reviews = await fetchProductReviews(product.id);
        appendReviews(product.id, reviews);
      } catch (error) {
        const reviewsDiv = document.getElementById(`reviews-${product.id}`)!;
        reviewsDiv.innerHTML = `<p class="error">⚠️ Error loading reviews: ${error}</p>`;
      }
    });

    try {
      const report = await fetchSalesReport();
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (error) {
      const errDiv = document.createElement("div");
      errDiv.className = "error";
      errDiv.textContent = `⚠️ Error loading sales report: ${error}`;
      output.appendChild(errDiv);
    }

  } catch (error) {
    output.innerHTML = `<p class="error">Fatal Error: ${error}</p>`;
  }
};

main();
```

USER:
in the css file where does it states the placeholder is going to be at the right?

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

ASSISTANT:
Great observation!

In the CSS file, the positioning of the **placeholder image to the right** is achieved using the `.product-header` rule:

```css
.product-header {
  display: flex;
  justify-content: space-between;
  align-items: center;
}
```

### 🔍 Here's how it works:
- `display: flex;` — Turns the container into a flexbox, allowing horizontal alignment of child elements.
- `justify-content: space-between;` — Pushes the first child (`<div>` with text) to the left and the second child (`<img>`) to the right.
- `align-items: center;` — Vertically centers the text and image in the same row.

This ensures the product details appear on the **left**, and the image placeholder floats neatly to the **right** inside the card.

If you'd like to tweak positioning further (e.g., padding/margin), we can refine it together.

ASSISTANT:
Great question! For an **image placeholder**, here are a few suitable options depending on your goal:

---

### ✅ **Types of Placeholder Images**

| Purpose | Example Image | Description |
|--------|----------------|-------------|
| **Generic product** | `https://via.placeholder.com/150` | A basic gray box with dimensions (e.g., 150x150). Good for testing. |
| **Product Not Found** | An icon like 🖼️ or "Image Coming Soon" | Useful if you want to signal a missing image. |
| **Themed placeholder** | Custom image like a blurred product photo or a branded “No Image” | Adds polish if you're aiming for professional UI. |
| **Local dev asset** | A file like `/assets/placeholder.png` | You can create/upload a simple PNG and reference it in the UI when needed. |

---

### 💡 Suggested Approach for This Project
Use a free placeholder service while building:

```ts
image: "https://via.placeholder.com/100"
```

Then replace it later with:

```ts
import placeholderImg from "../assets/placeholder.png"
```

(Once you have a local image file)

- [https://placeholder.com](https://placeholder.com)

- Or just make one in Canva with your preferred dimensions and text like "No Image".

### 🎯 Changes To Make:

### ✅ File 1: `frontend-parcel/main.ts` (Updated for loading indicators)

Paste this full content:
```ts
import "../frontend-parcel/style.css";
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport, Product } from "../src/apiSimulator";
import { retryPromise } from "../src/retryPromise";

// Output container
const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

// Render a single review
const renderReview = (container: HTMLElement, text: string, className = "review") => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = className;
  div.textContent = text;
  container.appendChild(div);
};

// Render product card
const renderProductCard = (product: Product) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";

  card.innerHTML = `
    <div class="card-content">
      <div class="product-details">
        <h2>${product.name}</h2>
        <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
        <h3>Reviews:</h3>
        <div class="loading">Fetching reviews...</div>
      </div>
    </div>
  `;

  output.appendChild(card);
  return card.querySelector(".product-details") as HTMLElement;
};

// Render sales report
const renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

// Show error block
const renderError = (msg: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = `Error: ${msg}`;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

// Footer
const renderFooter = () => {
  const footer = document.createElement("footer");
  footer.textContent = "© 2025 E-Commerce Dashboard Demo";
  document.body.appendChild(footer);
};

// Main async logic
const main = async () => {
  try {
    const loadingDiv = document.getElementById("loading");
    if (loadingDiv) loadingDiv.remove();

    const products = await retryPromise(fetchProductCatalog, 3, 1000);

    for (const product of products) {
      const card = renderProductCard(product);

      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);
        card.querySelector(".loading")?.remove();

        if (reviews.length === 0) {
          renderReview(card, "No reviews yet.");
        } else {
          reviews.forEach((r) => {
            renderReview(card, `💬 ${r.user}: ${r.comment}`);
          });
        }
      } catch (err) {
        card.querySelector(".loading")?.remove();
        renderReview(card, `⚠️ Failed to load reviews: ${err}`, "error");
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(fetchSalesReport, 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(`Failed to load sales report: ${err}`);
    }

    renderFooter();
  } catch (err) {
    const loadingDiv = document.getElementById("loading");
    if (loadingDiv) loadingDiv.remove();
    renderError(`${err}`);
  }
};

main();
```

```ts
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          {
            id: 1,
            name: "Laptop",
            price: 1200,
            image: new URL('./assets/placeholder.jpg', import.meta.url).toString()
          },
          {
            id: 2,
            name: "Headphones",
            price: 200,
            image: new URL('./assets/placeholder.jpg', import.meta.url).toString()
          }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

> 🧠 `new URL(..., import.meta.url).toString()` ensures that **Parcel bundles and rewrites the image path correctly**.

```ts
<img src="${product.image}" alt="${product.name}" class="product-image" />
```

ASSISTANT:
Here’s everything you need to **add the placeholder product image** using Parcel's bundling system:

---

### ✅ `frontend-parcel/apiSimulator.ts` (Full File with Image Support)

```ts
export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
  image: string;
}

// ✅ Load image using Parcel-compatible import
const placeholderImg = new URL('./assets/placeholder.jpg', import.meta.url).toString();

export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          {
            id: 1,
            name: "Laptop",
            price: 1200,
            image: placeholderImg
          },
          {
            id: 2,
            name: "Headphones",
            price: 200,
            image: placeholderImg
          }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

export const fetchProductReviews = (
  productId: number
): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`);
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{
  totalSales: number;
  unitsSold: number;
  averagePrice: number;
}> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({
          totalSales: 50000,
          unitsSold: 250,
          averagePrice: 200
        });
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch sales report");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

```ts
// --- apiSimulator.ts ---

export interface Product {
  id: number;
  name: string;
  price: number;
  image: string;
}

// ✅ Load images via Parcel-compatible URL imports
const laptopImg = new URL('./assets/laptop1.png', import.meta.url).toString();
const headphoneImg = new URL('./assets/headphone.png', import.meta.url).toString();

export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200, image: laptopImg },
          { id: 2, name: "Headphones", price: 200, image: headphoneImg }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

export const fetchProductReviews = (
  productId: number
): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`);
      }
    }, 1500);
  });
};

export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{
  totalSales: number;
  unitsSold: number;
  averagePrice: number;
}> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve({
          totalSales: 50000,
          unitsSold: 250,
          averagePrice: 200
        });
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch sales report");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

### ✅ `frontend-parcel/main.ts`

This version ensures images from `/assets` are used, and integrates the UI flow:

```ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from "../src/apiSimulator";
import { retryPromise } from "../src/retryPromise";

// DOM Elements
const output = document.getElementById("output")!;
const loading = document.getElementById("loading")!;

const renderReview = (container: HTMLElement, reviewText: string, className = "review") => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = className;
  div.textContent = reviewText;
  container.appendChild(div);
};

const renderProductCard = (product: { id: number; name: string; price: number }): HTMLElement => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <div class="card-content">
      <img src="./assets/${product.name.toLowerCase()}.png" alt="${product.name}" class="product-image" />
      <div class="product-details">
        <h2>${product.name}</h2>
        <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
        <h3>Reviews:</h3>
      </div>
    </div>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
  return card.querySelector(".product-details")!;
};

const renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

const renderError = (message: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = `Error: ${message}`;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

const renderFooter = () => {
  const footer = document.createElement("footer");
  footer.textContent = "Built with 💻 for Lab 2 - Promises & Error Handling";
  document.body.appendChild(footer);
};

const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);

    for (const product of products) {
      const container = renderProductCard(product);

      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);
        if (reviews.length === 0) {
          renderReview(container, "No reviews yet.");
        } else {
          reviews.forEach(r =>
            renderReview(container, `💬 ${r.user}: ${r.comment}`)
          );
        }
      } catch (err) {
        renderReview(container, `⚠️ ${err}`, "error");
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(String(err));
    }
  } catch (err) {
    renderError(String(err));
  } finally {
    loading.remove();
    renderFooter();
  }
};

// Start the app
main();
```

### ✅ Diagnosis

1. **Images Not Displaying**:
   - The `<img src="./assets/${product.name.toLowerCase()}.png" />` path assumes:
     - The images are named exactly like the `product.name.toLowerCase()` (e.g. `"laptop"` → `laptop.png`)
     - And they are located in `/frontend-parcel/assets/`
   - But from your earlier uploads, the files are:
     ```
     frontend-parcel/assets/headphone.png  ✅
     frontend-parcel/assets/laptop1.png ❌ ← This is the mismatch
     ```

2. **Image Placement**:
   - Images are appearing **on the left** because by default, `flex` aligns items left-to-right.
   - You want them **on the right**.

---

To match the current code logic, **rename `laptop1.png` → `laptop.png`**

```
/frontend-parcel/assets/laptop.png
```

- Works for static servers

```ts
const imageMap: Record<string, string> = {
```

### ✅ `frontend-parcel/main.ts`
```ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport } from "./apiSimulator";
import { retryPromise } from "../src/retryPromise";

// ✅ Import images so Parcel bundles them
import laptopImg from "./assets/laptop1.png";
import headphoneImg from "./assets/headphone.png";

// Image mapping by product name (normalized to lowercase)
const imageMap: Record<string, string> = {
  laptop: laptopImg,
  headphones: headphoneImg,
};

const output = document.getElementById("output")!;
const loading = document.getElementById("loading")!;

const renderReview = (container: HTMLElement, review: string, className = "review") => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = className;
  div.textContent = review;
  container.appendChild(div);
};

const renderProductCard = (product: { id: number; name: string; price: number }): HTMLElement => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";

  const imageUrl = imageMap[product.name.toLowerCase()] ?? "";

  card.innerHTML = `
    <div class="card-content" style="display: flex; justify-content: space-between; align-items: flex-start;">
      <div class="product-details">
        <h2>${product.name}</h2>
        <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
        <h3>Reviews:</h3>
      </div>
      <img src="${imageUrl}" alt="${product.name}" class="product-image" />
    </div>
  `;

  output.appendChild(card);
  return card.querySelector(".product-details")!;
};

const renderSalesReport = (report: {
  totalSales: number;
  unitsSold: number;
  averagePrice: number;
}) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

const renderError = (message: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = `Error: ${message}`;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);

    for (const product of products) {
      const productCard = renderProductCard(product);

      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);

        if (reviews.length === 0) {
          renderReview(productCard, "No reviews yet.");
        } else {
          reviews.forEach((r) => {
            renderReview(productCard, `💬 ${r.user}: ${r.comment}`);
          });
        }
      } catch (err) {
        renderReview(productCard, `⚠️ Error loading reviews: ${err}`, "error");
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(`Error fetching sales report: ${err}`);
    }
  } catch (err) {
    renderError(`Fatal Error: ${err}`);
  } finally {
    loading.remove(); // Hide loading message
  }
};

main();
```

ASSISTANT:
Here's your **corrected `main.ts`** file for **copy and paste**, with educational comments and the correct image paths:

```ts
// main.ts - Parcel frontend entry point

import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport, Product } from "./apiSimulator";
import { retryPromise } from "../src/retryPromise";

// ✅ Corrected image imports (ensure filenames match actual files)
import laptopImg from "./assets/laptop.png";
import headphoneImg from "./assets/headphone.png";

// Reference to loading and output elements
const loading = document.getElementById("loading")!;
const output = document.getElementById("output")!;

// Utility: render error message in red
const renderError = (msg: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = `Error: ${msg}`;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

// Utility: render individual review
const renderReview = (container: HTMLElement, text: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "review";
  div.textContent = text;
  container.appendChild(div);
};

// Render product card
const renderProduct = (product: Product, imageUrl: string) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";

  // Compose HTML
  card.innerHTML = `
    <div class="card-content" style="display: flex; justify-content: space-between;">
      <div class="product-details">
        <h2>${product.name}</h2>
        <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
        <h3>Reviews:</h3>
      </div>
      <img class="product-image" src="${imageUrl}" alt="${product.name}" />
    </div>
  `;

  output.appendChild(card);

  // Return the details div to append reviews
  return card.querySelector(".product-details") as HTMLElement;
};

// Render summary sales report
const renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
};

// Main app function
const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(fetchProductCatalog, 3, 1000);

    for (const product of products) {
      // Choose image based on product ID
      const image = product.name === "Laptop" ? laptopImg : headphoneImg;
      const productDiv = renderProduct(product, image);

      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);

        if (reviews.length === 0) {
          renderReview(productDiv, "No reviews yet.");
        } else {
          reviews.forEach((r) => renderReview(productDiv, `💬 ${r.user}: ${r.comment}`));
        }
      } catch (err) {
        renderReview(productDiv, `⚠️ Error loading reviews: ${err}`);
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(fetchSalesReport, 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(`Error loading sales report: ${err}`);
    }
  } catch (err) {
    renderError(`Fatal Error: ${err}`);
  } finally {
    loading.remove();
  }
};

main();
```

### ✅ `frontend-parcel/main.ts`

```ts
import { fetchProductCatalog, fetchProductReviews, fetchSalesReport, Product } from "./apiSimulator";
import { retryPromise } from "../src/retryPromise";

const output = document.getElementById("output")!;
const loading = document.getElementById("loading")!;

const renderReview = (container: HTMLElement, review: string, className = "review") => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = className;
  div.textContent = review;
  container.appendChild(div);
};

const renderProductCard = (product: Product): HTMLElement => {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";

  card.innerHTML = `
    <div class="product-details">
      <h2>${product.name}</h2>
      <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
      <h3>Reviews:</h3>
    </div>
  `;

  output.appendChild(card);
  return card.querySelector(".product-details")!;
};

const renderSalesReport = (report: { totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "card";
  div.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

const renderError = (message: string) => {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = message;
  output.appendChild(div);
};

const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);

    for (const product of products) {
      const productCard = renderProductCard(product);
      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductReviews(product.id), 3, 1000);
        if (reviews.length === 0) {
          renderReview(productCard, "No reviews yet.");
        } else {
          reviews.forEach((review) => {
            renderReview(productCard, `💬 ${review.user}: ${review.comment}`);
          });
        }
      } catch (err) {
        renderReview(productCard, `⚠️ Error loading reviews: ${err}`, "error");
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(`Error fetching sales report: ${err}`);
    }
  } catch (err) {
    renderError(`Fatal Error: ${err}`);
  } finally {
    loading.remove();
  }
};

main();
```

---

### ✅ `frontend-parcel/apiSimulator.ts`

```ts
import { Product } from "../src/index";

export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200 },
          { id: 2, name: "Headphones", price: 200 }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

export const fetchProductReviews = (productId: number): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.85) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." }
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`);
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{ totalSales: number; unitsSold: number; averagePrice: number }> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.9) {
        resolve({ totalSales: 50000, unitsSold: 250, averagePrice: 200 });
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch sales report");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

Update **`frontend-parcel/index.html`** to correct the stylesheet link:

#### 🔁 Replace:
```html
<link rel="stylesheet" href="../styles.css" />
```

#### ✅ With:
```html
<link rel="stylesheet" href="./style.css" />
```

This will correctly resolve the file relative to `frontend-parcel/index.html`, where `style.css` is located.

### ✅ `frontend-parcel/apiSimulator.ts` — **Final Version (Reviewed & Cleaned)**

```ts
import { Product } from "../src/index";

/**
 * Simulates fetching the product catalog with an 80% success rate.
 */
export const fetchProductCatalog = (): Promise<Product[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.8) {
        resolve([
          { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 1200 },
          { id: 2, name: "Headphones", price: 200 },
        ]);
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch product catalog");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

/**
 * Simulates fetching product reviews with an 85% success rate.
 */
export const fetchProductReviews = (
  productId: number
): Promise<{ user: string; comment: string }[]> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.85) {
        resolve([
          { user: "Alice", comment: "Great product!" },
          { user: "Bob", comment: "Very satisfied." },
        ]);
      } else {
        reject(`Failed to fetch reviews for product ID ${productId}`);
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};

/**
 * Simulates fetching the sales report with a 90% success rate.
 */
export const fetchSalesReport = (): Promise<{
  totalSales: number;
  unitsSold: number;
  averagePrice: number;
}> => {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    setTimeout(() => {
      if (Math.random() < 0.9) {
        resolve({ totalSales: 50000, unitsSold: 250, averagePrice: 200 });
      } else {
        reject("Failed to fetch sales report");
      }
    }, 1000);
  });
};
```

---

### ✅ `frontend-parcel/main.ts` — **Final Version (Simple UI Rendering)**

Make sure this file exists and includes proper rendering for catalog, reviews, and sales, along with error handling and styling. Here's a clean and educational version:

```ts
import {
  fetchProductCatalog,
  fetchProductReviews,
  fetchSalesReport,
} from "./apiSimulator";
import { retryPromise } from "../src/retryPromise";

// Get DOM references
const output = document.getElementById("output")!;
const loading = document.getElementById("loading")!;

/**
 * Displays an error block on the page.
 */
function renderError(message: string) {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "error";
  div.textContent = `Error: ${message}`;
  output.appendChild(div);
}

/**
 * Displays individual review inside a product card.
 */
function renderReview(container: HTMLElement, review: string) {
  const div = document.createElement("div");
  div.className = "review";
  div.textContent = review;
  container.appendChild(div);
}

/**
 * Displays a product card on the screen.
 */
function renderProductCard(product: { id: number; name: string; price: number }) {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";

  const productDetails = document.createElement("div");
  productDetails.className = "product-details";
  productDetails.innerHTML = `
    <h2>${product.name}</h2>
    <p><strong>Price:</strong> $${product.price}</p>
    <h3>Reviews:</h3>
  `;

  card.appendChild(productDetails);
  output.appendChild(card);

  return productDetails;
}

/**
 * Displays the final sales report.
 */
function renderSalesReport(report: {
  totalSales: number;
  unitsSold: number;
  averagePrice: number;
}) {
  const card = document.createElement("div");
  card.className = "card";
  card.innerHTML = `
    <h2>Sales Report</h2>
    <p><strong>Total Sales:</strong> $${report.totalSales}</p>
    <p><strong>Units Sold:</strong> ${report.unitsSold}</p>
    <p><strong>Average Price:</strong> $${report.averagePrice}</p>
  `;
  output.appendChild(card);
}

/**
 * Main app logic - handles all UI and API logic.
 */
const main = async () => {
  try {
    const products = await retryPromise(() => fetchProductCatalog(), 3, 1000);

    for (const product of products) {
      const container = renderProductCard(product);

      try {
        const reviews = await retryPromise(
          () => fetchProductReviews(product.id),
          3,
          1000
        );

        reviews.forEach((r) =>
          renderReview(container, `💬 ${r.user}: ${r.comment}`)
        );
      } catch (err) {
        renderReview(container, `⚠️ ${err}`);
      }
    }

    try {
      const report = await retryPromise(() => fetchSalesReport(), 3, 1000);
      renderSalesReport(report);
    } catch (err) {
      renderError(`${err}`);
    }
  } catch (err) {
    renderError(`Fatal Error: ${err}`);
  } finally {
    loading.remove();
  }
};

main();
```

```css
  color: #900;
  margin-top: 0.5rem;
  padding: 0.5rem;
  border-left: 4px solid darkred;
  border-radius: 4px;
}

  text-align: center;
  font-style: italic;
  color: #666;
}

  text-align: center;
  margin-top: 2rem;
  padding-top: 1rem;
  border-top: 1px solid #ccc;
  color: #888;
  font-size: 0.9rem;
}
```

ASSISTANT:
If your `README.md` file isn't displaying on your GitHub repository's main page, here are some steps to troubleshoot and resolve the issue:

---

### ✅ 1. **Ensure the File Is Named Correctly**

GitHub is case-sensitive regarding filenames. The file must be named exactly `README.md` (all uppercase letters for "README" and lowercase for ".md"). Files named `readme.md`, `ReadMe.md`, or any other variation may not be recognized properly.

---

### ✅ 2. **Verify the File Is in the Root Directory**

For GitHub to display the `README.md` on the repository's main page, the file must be located in the root directory of your repository. If it's placed inside a subdirectory (e.g., `docs/README.md`), it won't appear on the main page.

---

### ✅ 3. **Check That the File Is Not Empty**

An empty `README.md` file may not be rendered by GitHub. Ensure that the file contains some content, even if it's just a placeholder text.

---

### ✅ 4. **Confirm the File Is Tracked by Git**

Run the following command to check if `README.md` is being tracked:

```bash
git ls-files | grep -i readme.md
```

If it doesn't appear in the list, add it:

```bash
git add README.md
git commit -m "Add README.md"
git push origin main
```

Replace `main` with your branch name if different.

---

### ✅ 5. **Refresh the GitHub Page**

Sometimes, GitHub may take a moment to update the repository view. Try refreshing the page after a few minutes to see if the `README.md` appears.

---

If you've followed all these steps and the `README.md` still doesn't display, please provide more details about your repository structure or any error messages you're encountering, and I'll be glad to assist further.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
